Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not better, as it is commanded in the dance, she should soak her left hand in oil of sesame or in alum, and then put it back in its place.</start_of_turn>
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and grasp the second; and when she has found it, if she grasps it and extends it back and forth, so that the mark does not bleed during the extraction.</start_of_turn
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move lightly to and fro, and then treat her; for it will come out and dry up.</start_of_turn>
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is loose, as we have said, for the cure we have mentioned, of stopping the bleeding and fumigating herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that we have said, if you do not follow our advice;

Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument in which we fumigate the woman at the retention of the flowers and the secondine if it is thus:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen like a vine, and one puts on the head of the instrument over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	or let the fumigations be over the charcoal, and the tinder until it is consumed, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	For one must pierce the foundation which has not properly grasped the basis, since the latter has been stifled by some subtle spasm.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	If it is necessary, therefore, to break that spasm which has grasped the basis, and do not pierce with any sudden violence, but keep the incision firm so that it does not move;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on moist lint soaked in wine and oil, and then apply the bandage until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, if you put or remove a weight of lead, and you leave the hands motionless, and be still as when the boy saw the hare in the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Under no circumstances does this stupid fellow come to the rescue of a wound or an abscess; if you must cover this up, if either it be cured or as we have said, with a weight of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	from the foundation of the fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that arise from the foundation are nodular and grow greater when they arise from below the foundation, or between the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or several; and when that swelling is ancient, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture which is white or slightly yellow,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	If there is never any healing of these fistulas; and they are known by the fact that there is discharge or flatulence when the patient discharges, and by chance there is a wound.</start_of_turn>
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach up to the hip joint, and up to the navel.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the persistent fistula at its foundation, and does not disappear.</start_of_turn
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite your thumb or foundation, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, if you insert a slight attempt of sponge, or horsehair, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair at your thumb;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no bleeding, swelling or wind, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	it does not pierce the skin; if you are in a hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists until the bladder or the urine duct, if in a jump the urine escapes and cannot be retained by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is perceived until the hip joint, if the vein is twisted up to the root;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no swelling and no sign of pain, if it is only necessary to bow a little, and there is no benefit from medicine or support by ointment;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no other cure than work, and vanity of the fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is neither new nor old, hope for health by fire, as I have seen.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and keep his legs stretched out to his thighs, and has his thighs leaning towards his belly
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then make an attempt to strain, or plunge if there is pain, until you feel the bone snap or the attempt comes.

se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	He feels that he has already perceived it; and whether it is uncovered or you feel between your shoulder and the armpit, the limb is stiff and its bones creak.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not slip away, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We can do almost anything well without them, but this is not the case;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help of this, if one does not handle the fire cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it is said beforehand;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And the remainder of the boils all rise up in the fistula, as far as they come down from the foundation; and do this once or twice, until you know that these boils must be burned, which are like a cluster of bees.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Then the doctor should apply moist compresses to the boil, until the boils are burst; then he should cauterize the area around the boil with oil, while holding the wound closed.</start_of_turn>
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus well, it is good. But if not, it will not be well.</start_of_turn>
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule à ce qui enseut la coverture dou keur.

Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he does not go away of himself, and stands between you and the work, let the fire cautery or the medicine suffice.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together these two things: namely, the burning of these hairy things, the stopping of blood and the drying out of moisture

puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	When the fire is extinguished, do not leave it on the body for longer than is necessary to complete the task.

When the fistula comes up to the surface of the skin and is loosened from its root, if the thumb or the foundation is grasped or displaced, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Emorrydes are of two kinds: when they are deep-seated in the foundation, like grains of resin, and are small and large in number, and cut across exactly without causing damage, they are harmless.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more of them, and extend beyond the foundation and the root of the limb; but those which extend beyond have moisture in them
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and are yellow-brown in color or have the color of citrine or blood, and are soft; ou plus souvent elles sont de taille grande et se trouvent au milieu du corps, ou au-dessus des os, et s’étend jusqu’à la pointe du corps, ou plus loin.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have it in the foundation, if you command the patient to sigh and go to bed, as long as the foundations are firm, and uncover the child;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and hold it with your nails, or grasp it with your finger, then push it into its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if it will not stay put by its moisture, if you take hold of it with cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and draw them toward your shoulders, then push them, and powder under them warm powders that are in lieu of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or thou cauterisest them as it is said or captain of cautery, and then thou curest them of other cures while they be sound.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the foundation cannot be retained, if thou clenchest the patient by the teeth firmly biting and grasping, so as to remove that which is or is the foundation, if it can be retained openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	the patient cannot suffer, and if the thread is for the foundation, if it is the slight cure;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that thou grasp them with thy nail or tweezers, and hold them firm, and then cure them as we have said, while they be sound, and that thou fear not the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you command the suture thus: take one thread and pierce it with a needle, then pass the thread through the underside and draw out the needle from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread around the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	If you command the suture thus: take one thread and pierce it with a needle, then pass the thread through the underside and draw out the needle from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread around the needle; if the thread is too large, hold the thread firm, then pass the needle through, and draw out the needle along with some of the thread; leave one inch to correct the excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation one moist bandage in rose oil or beeswax, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it until it quiets down, and when it has quieted, if the treatment for swelling and other treatments are complete, while he is still sane.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Then leave it until it quiets down, and when it has quieted, if the treatment for swelling and other treatments are complete, while he is still sane.</start_of_turn>

dou fremit	But let him rest.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice is a small outgrowth that grows before the body, and will move about in the body.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And never does it cease to move, and it is felt just as if dead weight, and comes to every part of the body, more than in any other place.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure for this is if you take a pin of goose feather or a strong pin of bull, and put that pin on the weight, as long as the weight circles around the weight all around
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all the way around the weight until you cover it all around, and put it in the middle, and pull the weight out from its roots.

ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere. Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and large if it is very wide, or the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a swelling or the belly is bound, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced at one side and at the other side; and has at one of the ribs, that is to say, pierced, and at the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and either the belly or the doctor puts medicines in a bladder of good leather or parchment, and either pierces all around the wounds,

et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	When the medicine is finished, if the thread has in front of it a strong thread, then clinch; and that is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Neither too hot nor too cold should the medicine be; and join the head of the clinch with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and then bind it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then grasp the minister with his two hands assembled, until it is all visible, then withdraw the clinch, and let the patient rest his legs at leisure,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	If the medicine sees that it is urgent, if the pain is great as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night without relief, that is a greater help.

Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	If swelling is at the root or the base, or in the wound, if it is as subtle as with a child.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is how the subtle swelling appears when the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous section the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicines, as appropriate.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the nature of the wound or the part that is wounded, and from how they are made.</start_of_turn
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are by biting of stone, and of the size of a spear or nail, or of an arrow or lance or fist or knife, or similar things.</start_of_turn
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	When things are done according to custom, as with wounds that occur on the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you of the cure for a wound on the head, and I shall begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come back to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or a wound on the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no chipping of bone or other things, and the skin is completely ruptured and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you must doubt the cautery of the head: if you do it too soon after the wound, if there is blood from the wound, or on the contrary from the part above;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And hear the patient drink wine and raw flesh to repletion.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	Or if he does not feel better, if he is faint or does not drink wine, does not eat meat, do not let him eat bread;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put out the wound, if there is swelling, cover it with a soft compress soaked in rose oil or wine styptic;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, if put on the wound, if it is fresh at all its extent, and is not moved by the air, powder, that I will tell you about later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it has moved already, put on some ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large, like a saw cut and similar, and the edges do not reunite by themselves, if you reunite them with stitches, like when I say wounds on the belly, with stitches.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered by bone, and is gaping, and holds only at a point, if it be so; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin.</start_of_turn>
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat raw meats, such as testicles and barley, as well as poultry, and similar things.</start_of_turn
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find or cut through bone that does not belong there, grasp it firmly, pull it out, and then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	If there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be held by remedies, if you find the artery, and if you see that it is dislocated, grasp it with a thread.</start_of_turn>
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If that does not help, cauterize it.</start_of_turn>

Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And thus is the manner of the powder: take incense, one part; dragon's blood, three parts; live charcoal, two parts, and mix them together.

et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting:

si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if he is reset according to his natural form in his own place.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	for this is dangerous, because it is worth dying for.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	If it is certain that you are managing the patient on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and raise his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	when they are in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	and puts the head and the arm higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And thus if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts.

et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus I command you to do what I have said in great and moist wounds.</start_of_turn>

puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then leave the head of the wound, that is to say, at a distance, and pierce with a needle or if there is any strong thread;

qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is soaked through the leather, as long as you make it pierce from that part,

puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	Then the strain of a double thread around the needle’s eye,

tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all wounds are restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are blunt, between soft and hard,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the blunt needles cover all the hair, and the too thick ones do not penetrate well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason, it is advised that they be soft.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not be forced too deeply into the flesh and skin,

et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching is more suitable for small wounds.</start_of_turn

Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second dressing is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and is that you put together the hairs of the leather and the hairs of the silk together with a needle or there is much strong thread in the middle.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these things thoroughly together.</start_of_turn

Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of cautery, which Galiens does properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is such that no one does like him, who assemble the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	And they seize one of the chiefs with the other chief, in part manner:

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgements of the wound are the same as the judgements of other wounds:

Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	The liquid that flows from any wound or incision, when it becomes visible, is called a fistula.</start_of_turn
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	And the same, when it is crooked and bent inwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is like true, the nodulation must be firm and white, or we do not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is as crooked as the quill of a pen;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never in clear water, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Never once, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it elsewhere in the treatment of wounds, that every wound that is not cleansed, and there is no pus,

c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of the blood or bone;
ou por sa malice;	ou por sa malice;

car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture is short from one hole to another, and fills the cavity;

et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	I will tell you of a fistula that had a home in the leg of a man,</start_of_turn
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you can take example of it and help in your work.</start_of_turn>
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	It was once a young man about .xxx. years of age, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the matters came to the limb, and fled from a great abscess, and there was no cause to fear from opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but they made their mark on the abscess more than on the opening of the wound,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and there came out moisture from matters, and became a fistula, and there came out moisture from the wound that all went well and moist with blood;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	And they remain for a year, and there is no wise man in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I remind them, and see their limb and the medicines which were used for them.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and this which was cured by the physicians was with great cost;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red like blood, and had the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I attempted a cure in one of these wounds, and then I bound all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I attempted a cure in one of these wounds, and then I found that one wound was finding the other throughout the whole limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened and closed one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I found it corrupted and putrefying, and the corruption went up to the bone itself;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I suffer that which appears to me of a corrupted bone, and I care for nothing else but that which I see;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I commence to restore the wound with healing herbs for a long time, but I cannot bind it together.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began to uncover the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found that there was a great corruption of blood in the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	But I cannot do more than I can grasp with my hand, and the traitor will force me to his full measure.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	Then I restored the medicines; and he was healed and became sound and healthy again
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and did not want to repeat the work for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death which I avoid for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often is blood evacuated with the opening of a vein, but they remained whole and sound.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And in place of the bone there was a hard scale, and it was in good position and not at all in discomfort, neither upward nor downward, neither to the left nor to the right.</start_of_turn>
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in no place of bone, if you must cover it in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one thread and strain it at the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	And command him not to extend it upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	And put another layer of linen thicker than the first one, and bind it upon the limb which is beyond the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head, so that you break the corrupt marrow at the break.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the limb above the bone or where you see marrow, so that it does not break the bone;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put a bandage or a weight of lead on the bone to hold the corrupted flesh covered with the skin.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And cover so much as you can see and feel the corruption, and cover again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh completely; then put a weight of lead on it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then some part of the body corrupts from one end to the other, or the corruption persists for a long time, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	If the corruption is in the joint, if the corrupted joint is grasped and the bone or what it contains on the other side is grasped;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	If the corruption is in the continuation of the joints, if there is no other vessel but that of covering.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	If the corruption is or the palm of the hand, or the heel, if it is very strong in that thing;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	But indeed you must inquire about that corrosion, how it breaks open.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and handle it in every way you wish, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and that the stitches that you make and the threads to cover these bones are many, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of swelling.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their greatness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to show some resemblance of work to deceive his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and such tools that the work will show the instrument that you must have, according to the knowledge of this art.</start_of_turn>
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think the instrument that you must have according to this is sufficient.
dou feu	Dou feu
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	Dou feu
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	Dou feu
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	Dou feu
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient escapes by this death or by malice, which is greater, from the fault of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards comes corruption of the limb in limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes by all the body; if you delay with the covering,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it is by the percussion of venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea, vipers, and the like,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	And if it is by the percussion of venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea, vipers, and the like, the wound will be at the head of the bone, if it swells, and will not allow it to move until the hand arrives.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the bone is at the joint, so that the dislocation does not reach the forearm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the forearm, if the bone is against the flesh; and if it passes the flesh, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And only the outer measure of safety is the amount of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do as much as when corrosion comes or burns: if it comes to the first joint, if the other joint follows afterwards;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or burns, if it burns all the burn;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the limb, if it burns at the joint of the elbow;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	If it comes from below the knee, if there is no other ailment but that the patient be left to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of covering or binding the limb if you bind it below and above,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	extend one finger of the lower limb, and another finger of the upper limb,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	you will dry the flesh that is between the two limbs to a space of about the width of a hazelnut, as much as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then the cap or scapula, and put a cushion there, namely a strip of linen, so that the scapula does not touch the sound limb.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and come to the patient other lesion and incision of the flesh.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	and blood comes out when you work; if you cauterize the limb enough,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then join the limb steadily with a firm ligament, and cure it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there is one home in the foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	there was a black spot that seemed like fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion first came out of its heel, so that it scorched the whole foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the bone is seen to be corroded, if it is covered with earth, and is sound;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	it lasts long after the return of the corruption or two hands, and comes back to me.</start_of_turn>
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put upon it things that rebound after the corruption has been expelled, and I cannot stop the corruption.</start_of_turn>
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and I take leave that I break my hand, and I would rather avoid the hope of recovering the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And I also doubt that if I were to cut off his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he fainted completely, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and as for covering his hand, he was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have heard of nothing else concerning this matter except for this.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never comes a vein to an abscess in vain, and it lingers so long that it makes great assembly of blood.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then breaks and bursts, and in the jump makes blood clot, and lingers the pus, just as if blood vessels had been broken;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is underneath is also as soft as torn silk
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And it is not called a fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so elongated that it reaches the bone under the skin, it is called a fistula.</start_of_turn>
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the wound is such that you must hold the skin all around, and even when it is subtle, like a drape.</start_of_turn
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	If you suspect that the skin is rotting and the corruption is not apparent on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	If the skin is thick with pus, when the surgeon cuts into it:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	watch if there is much discharge, and if it smells like foul air,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then apply Egyptian medicine plaster which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take ease, and oil, and lard, equally, and mix well in one vessel over the fire.

et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and mix well the liquid, and restrain the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine for three hours, then extract it while breathing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do it quickly, until the pain has subsided and the swelling has gone down.</start_of_turn>
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	never mix it with vinegar.</start_of_turn
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not there, and you take wine vinegar, and drink water from below.</start_of_turn>
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then the pulse, and in clinking, as long as you can tell that the veins are well closed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither Egyptian medicine with its unguents will help him.</start_of_turn>
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if there is an abundance of water and honey or there is a little bit of bruised barley.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you bathe with honey and wine, because honey has the property of softening and washing away.</start_of_turn
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	And the wine makes the blood red.

et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the opening of the wound is below the belly, if the edge or the root lies lower than it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is in pain, if there is no swelling to hold it back;

Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the shoulder joint suddenly feels loose and dislocates after remaining taut for a while, the bones that make up the shoulder do not retain their normal position.

quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When the limb is not affected by any disease,

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure for fistula is not completed as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	De l’aposteme de l’ungle.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	From the apex of the shoulder
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from the bone, or by chance it arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is envious, and one does not take care, if it comes it brings about a shoulder dislocation.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And immediately grasp the bow and hold it until it reaches the root of the bone, and by chance grasp it all;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And there comes corrosion until the bone, until there comes sharp pain, and the head of the bone is swollen and pale.</start_of_turn>
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help.</start_of_turn
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must take away all the superfluousness that is hindering the bone.</start_of_turn
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is great help when the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses the hair inwards, and the wound begins to swell, and blood appears,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must know that you must leave only the root of the hair that points outwards.

puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound until it is healed.

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be great.</start_of_turn>
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	and two thumbs do appear in the hands of some people by chance are all callous,

Des vils	Villages.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Village villages are blood vessels enclosed in fluid that is full of melancholy humours, which cause pain in many limbs.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often there is in the leg of those who walk and work and carry burdens, than among others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	And thus you must not give them any sudden expulsion of bile, but then the remainder of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is as follows: two methods: one is with vinegar, and treat the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other method is to bind the vein and pull it out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size should be such that: first of all, the acute limb is strongly warmed, until the large one is not scorched without being softened.

puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then relieve and drain the black blood from your hand, from the one shoulder to the other, as much as the patient can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then the leech, and he commands that he hold beef jerky clinging to black soot.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And he recommences the evacuation and the blood when the veins are full, and harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The food of the sick is as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it out or bathe it, and let the limb of the patient become warm as red as the veins expand;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, if the fire is strong, then hold the edge of the vein over the long belly or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then press the skin over the abscess, and support the belly from below, until it bursts when you feel it
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out or the skin appears just like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then stretch the wound, until it is freed from the skin, and then close it with the thumb.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then take hold of the limb in another place two fingers distant; then stretch the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then hold the limb steady as before, and grasp it with another hand, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take hold of the limb in another place two fingers distant; then stretch the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then take hold of the limb in another place two fingers distant; then stretch the skin over the vein until it appears.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you do not handle and lift it, if there is a splinter of any kind of strong double thread at all.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And hold the splinter firmly with one hand and grasp the other end with the other hand, until it comes out completely.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep that it does not break, for if it breaks, if cannot be treated or lifted, and comes to harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it, put out the limb from the wound with clean wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and surrounded altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and surrounded altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must force it open violently, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of force which we use to open the eye if it is curved, and do not pierce, but only to hold the eye;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	...so large that if it were slight, it would pierce the pupil, but as it is large as we have said, this is the form.
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the leg, in hot regions where there is no grass or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it occurs elsewhere except in the leg, and this comes from corruption that comes from the decay of the leather.</start_of_turn>
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes from the belly towards the back, between the skin and the flesh.

et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, if you break off a part, and cover the remainder, and do not cover it to its root, until it is fully healed;

por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it must be treated openly and left open until it is completely healed, and nothing remains or crusts over.</start_of_turn>
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and never is this vein treated when it is cut through five palm-widths or more.</start_of_turn

And one hand came to me, from ten palms of length, and when you grasp it, if there be one hair or a wound, and pierce to the bone; if all is well, then empty the matter that is within, and bring to the hand medicines that cause no harm, and then cure as with abscesses.
