Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From the hair that grows between skin and bone
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This ailment is called in our land "buffalo disease", because it often causes swelling of the buttocks.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small hair that grows between skin and bone, and goes up and down all over the body,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it is often felt on one or more limbs, as far as the skin or flesh is pulled or stretched.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infected with the putrefaction of some humors, as when they come towards and surround the worms, light and dark, or ascarides, or the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and there is doubt of its malice, for when it goes through the flesh and reaches the head, it comes to the marrow,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it returns through chance, and destroys the marrow; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot drive it out until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	If it is certain, then hold the limb above and bind it securely with a strong and tight ligature.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then grasp above and pull firmly, and if it is grasped by the flesh in the armpit, and you do not see it move,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if the fire cautery is done above, until it turns black;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harms that it makes are when it comes into contact with oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	If you see it coming or near the oil, if the nails are strained, pluck out the hair above, then grasp above and pull forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And you must instruct the patient to use diverse external medications of resolving character to expel harmful humors carried by the blood
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And take care of nourishing the patient with nourishing foods that promote healing.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind-relatedness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and thus it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this which I tell you.</start_of_turn>
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I went to a woman who was sick, and discovered a small swelling in the armpit of her arm.</start_of_turn
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and thus it grew up like a worm on her shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	More painful than anything else, even as much as living silver when it cuts through flesh.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain comes from that limb itself, and extends into the shoulder blade.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards corrected throughout the limb, as far as it goes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it was told to me that it twisted back inwards of the limb, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how she moves limb against limb, for I have never seen such a disease according to this method.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I must avoid wanting to move the pain from one limb to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I must not wish to do so, as I see her do in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I think that this is because the woman has dry skin and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And thus appeared that constraint of that windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear with me according to this reason to those who are pleasing, and who have moist bodies and veins restored.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	and when you see that this sickness is cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the limb hangs limp and heavy, and then suddenly recovers as much as that constraint of the windiness is released;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	Et cautérise le leu; et si tu ne la vois à tes yeux,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
Des saiettes	From sponges.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Sponges are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body where they are used.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their hairs is such that some are large-pointed, others small, and some have chews and sowdies.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have three angles, others have tongues, and some have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	or in the main it chews, and that is the worst way to chew; or in the foot it chews, and that is the second worst way to chew,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	so that it can never make use of them again.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When the limb hangs limp and death is imminent, know that I will tell you later, when I have learned, what the sign is.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you are aware that the arrow must be extracted, for death follows in many disorders;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this sign does not appear, neither does the arrow pierce the flesh, if the limb is properly treated and the wound is cured.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	The sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone, and the blood spurts from the vein which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	Est que scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	When vomiting and soiling and spitting and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of wits, and vomiting of bile; and by chance there are no nails or ears; and by chance the speech and voice are lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And a leap from the wound white resembling a pulse, and in the leap as also with brown soot;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear to you, if you stay with the cure, and take away the bandage if it is not necessary.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of a fracture when it breaks or curves, is that it is close to the left breast, and feels just as if it were fixed in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the fracture moves just like a pulse, and blood spurts black without, cold sweat and cold fainting, and loss of consciousness.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then there is doubt that death approaches
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the fracture that never leaves without pain is that the wound swells, the throat is inflamed, the patient turns pale, and breathing is difficult and gasping for air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the splinter breaks in the palm of the hand, if it is removed with small nails; it causes great pain and swelling and breathing difficulty; and all the limb is stiff.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the splinter breaks or is in the stomach, by chance if it comes out without any indigestible meat of the body.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the splinter breaks or is in the stomach, and by chance comes out without any stool from the intestine, if there is no hope for the cure, do not attempt to extract the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the splinter breaks in the bladder, and the urine comes out in spurts and comes out with difficulty, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it be made and the collarbone and the throat and the shoulder and the elbow and the wrist and the forearm and the hand, and the like of them, are all subject to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the tendon is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this I have seen that you do other things.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was once a woman who had a splinter or a piece of mucus at the root of her tooth.</start_of_turn
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and from the other side I squeezed the fat of the ear, and it was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And from there I extracted a sliver that had lodged in the fat of the ear, from the root to the tip.</start_of_turn>
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the sliver was restored, and only the tip remained visible.</start_of_turn
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and it was a sliver like a Turkish arch, all of it very thin in the ear; the pain was gone, and there was no further discomfort.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take out a splinter from the throat to a crestian, and the Arabian lance was in the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I extracted the thorns, and I withdrew it as long as I could, and the crestian was healed.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I took out a splinter from his side, which was in the belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after a few days, he recovered his composure;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the splinter, and the nail, and the thread, and not at all a bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if thus be the case where a splinter has fallen into the eye or lies deep under the skin;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and do not hold back its natural inclinations,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	One will find no solace in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And thus another man, who had an arrow lodged in his cheek, was sewn up the wound.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and suffered great pain; and there were other symptoms as well.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And carried an arrow to a prince of the royal house, who had it stuck sideways in his nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely withdrawn.</start_of_turn>
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I must depart from healing after that which has lasted two days. If I find the wound much swollen.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I must depart from healing after that which has lasted two days. If I find the wound much swollen. I will attempt to treat it with all my might, and I do not feel it myself;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there is no longer any sensation of pain or tingling.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that this was the tip of an arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place upon the limb a plaster that is both adhesive and digestive, so that it does not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I see the limb become pale from the wound
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster immediately, and closed the wound again, and reassured the patient for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the pain of the wound again; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put the caustic medicine on the wound with my hands every day, until it was well healed.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and held the eye shut, and felt the head of the splinter which was coming out at the root;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I closed the wound with that caustic medicine, until the splinter was visibly coming out.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it lasted three months in all
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then expand if the wound allows, and I will bind the teeth firmly from one side and the other, and I cannot do otherwise.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I will continue to toil and devise means, as long as I take hold of it, that is to say, as long as the teeth are well bound,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	since this is the form that will be at the end of this chapter, as long as I hold it, and I will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And it is judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it immediately, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or tell me of the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your remedy on that which I do not understand, because the books do not teach me all;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you know the masters better than anyone about great things, and about that which is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Trueve neuf Chapitre, et neuf instrument, au descendant des choses estranges qui arrivent en cet art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	Nine new chapters and nine new instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	for either by liquid or by other means.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes out by itself from the flesh, that is to say, the saivet that is intrans in the flesh, must never come out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not happen at once, if you leave it as long as the hair is carried along, and rejoice at the issue;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is caught in the bone and cannot be freed, if you leave it for a few days, and move it every day.</start_of_turn>
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, if you prick around with all sorts of subtle things, as long as the limb is swollen, and then withdraw it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	and if the bone at the head of the shoulder is fractured, and goes right up to one of the bellies of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And concerning any other accident that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not treat it immediately, but leave it as it is until it is even again after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if it comes to the bone just below the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	it is only bruised on the bone itself, and does not come to the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains sore for several days, even after the bad accident has passed, if the wound is not treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is firmly fixed and cannot be moved, if you administer tarres around it as I have said; then cure the limb once it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	If the swelling is restored to the limb despite its pain, if we cannot see it, if it has all its strength; then it is cured once it has completely healed.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if the limb has no obvious blemish;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you do not see the wound, and if the swelling is deep,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and if there is an ear in the wound, as it holds it there.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the flesh that is stuck to the bone is pulled out with the wound
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or crush the ears of the bandage, as long as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take care that though you do not break the splinter, you grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not grasp it at once, if the splinter remains fixed in the wound, grasp it firmly, for its extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If the bleeding from the wound contradicts your treatment, take heed of what is written in this chapter concerning the cure.</start_of_turn>
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	Beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and take care that you do not further irritate the splinter.</start_of_turn
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Or thrust, or tear, or firmly or mildly; and set the patient according to the shape as when the arrow flew in,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Or thrust, or tear, or firmly or mildly; and set the patient according to the shape as when the arrow flew in, for this is the greatest help that is, and if you do not know how, if you do not understand what it shows you, do as it shows you.</start_of_turn>
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or there is no wound, or the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore, hold it there until the nails can grasp it, and then remove the arrow: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it [the dislocation] is held in the bone, if you round your hand around the bone until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be moved, if you leave it fixed, and then resume the extraction until it comes out naturally.</start_of_turn>
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow stuck in it, if you remove it all at once.</start_of_turn>
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is pain, and you see it administered immediately, if it is administered with a blunt instrument.</start_of_turn
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the tip of the arrow enters the socket of the instrument; and then you must force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If the arrow is deeply embedded, force the instrument’s pointed end into the wound to facilitate its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	If the arrow is surrounded, if you can, remove all surrounding tissue or the poison, if that is what you wish,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then cure the wound as you deem necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the splinter is in the eye or on the foot or in the belly or in the bladder or in the chest, and it is close, and you can cover over it, cover it over.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	cover the wound and the nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to treat the splinters is like a bird's beak, and thus is this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the end of the bone is like the quill of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to push out the tip of the arrow, as is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps to push and to grasp is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common size.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins of common size.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	From veins of common size.
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	From veins of common size.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And thus veins that are in the armpits of the eyes, which are called "aspires,"
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the brow and the vein that is at the back of the head.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the armpits of the eyes;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the veins that are under the chin and those that are under the lips, which are called "augeherich."
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And thus veins that are swollen throughout their length.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	Those veins which we commonly see swollen throughout their length are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which runs alongside the left costal cartilage, and is often called the great vein of the arm.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it the vein of the head, and if it is swollen or distended at the cost,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the vein of the head, and if it is swollen or distended at the cost.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one which is always open to the outside, which appears immediately above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation is the vein which is between the thumb and the index finger, and if there is rain;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the limb or the palm of the hand are two veins: one if it is severed by the corbicula of the pocket of the left costal rib.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second is that which is at the ankle of the right costal rib; and the vein which is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other costal rib.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are two veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to remove old blood clots, and prevents them from forming again.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of the patient, as I have said, is that you must rejoice at the chief of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the limb or the veins are of a rough texture; then tighten the patient’s collar with a knot.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the veins open behind the ears depend from the chief:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	give attention to your duty, and where you feel the pulse of your duty, if it be a sign of madness;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet, and holding it by the handle, pierce the vein up to the bone, then keep your hand firm on the upper part of the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then clamp and ligate the skin and the vein well. It must traverse two thumbs. Make blood flow until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and tie it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and soaks, and causes the eyes to overflow with tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the blood is so like that which I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient's head is strained, as the two veins open widely.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse of his thumb, and then he seizes it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then he places his hand on the vein in his palm at the base of his thumb, and grasps the lancet of his thumb.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and he grasps the vein upwards, and holds it firmly, as you have done with other veins, and evacuate blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then he releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, and then puts on a bandage.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then the thread comes, and it is left as long as it remains whole; and as for it, we have already spoken of it and its handling and its extraction, or its beginning from the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the head; and it has diseases of the ancient face, and emigration, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	When the patient’s head is twisted, the vein bursts open;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called the “forceps,” which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and keep your hand firm, or something else, and let blood flow out as much as you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient’s collar and tie the vein until it is firm and never do the work with a wide flame.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for me to say that the flame should be too thick; and the same with the other side, because the bone is close, and by chance the flame breaks the bone when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the armpits that are in the armpits is helpful for the eruptions, and for the swelling, and for the redness, and for the hair, and there are diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And if the patient strains his neck by turning his head to one side, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the same, and let the blood drain slowly, a little at a time, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is feeble, by chance if it breaks; then make an incision for the blood to escape, as much as you are able, and then bind it up tightly with a bandage, and press it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood from the vein does not taste like water, and has a strong scent of sickness, and is subject to fainting spells.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If there is swelling and redness that comes to the face, and even if it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	if there is also a bleeding of the blood if the patient bites his throat, then strain his neck to your left hand.</start_of_turn>
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the small flame long, and put it on the lip between the two nostrils.</start_of_turn>
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open very well immediately, and it will not begin to heal now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far from the wound, but rather correct the blood according to your need; then bind it for the night, for it is usually restored by morning.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And that is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the .ij. guindeges helps to restrain the swelling, and to start the process of healing, and to cure diseases, and to expel worms, and to corrode, and to cause herpes, and to cause dysentery.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the blood is that if the patient pulls out his head from the nose with one hand and with the other hand, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And either the master stands above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a chair.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then hold the vein long and widely open, and prick the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same on the other vein, and loosen the thread, and restrain the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the liver above helps to cause swelling in the mouth, corruption of the gums, ulcers of the liver, and vomiting and pain.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are known by this, that they are black, and because they have small black veins running through them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So do one with the other, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt,

De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the bottom of the tongue to the nails.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are soaked with moisture if it helps after the bleeding of the cephalic [vein], and that is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth.

saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then drain both of them [the veins] and do not leave too much blood in them, for there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which commonly cause us concern are often healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking at their root with a burning flame, or with an olive twig as thin as needles, which is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame that is made with a mirror is known as "mirtin", and is large as you see it:

et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and thus resembles a olive flame.</start_of_turn>

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with the ailments that are nausea of the throat, and swelling of the jaw, and pain in the belly;

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of the vein helps to stop the pain of the head and the swelling of the body.

et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is useful to the health that it flows through the nerve that is below, and if it does not flow too much, and it finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the health is either crippled or by chance cannot be healed.
